<div class="slide titlepage">
<h1 class="title">Measures of Central Tendency and Dispersion</h1>
<p class="author">
Simon J. Kiss
</p>
<p class="date">17/03/2020</p>
</div>
<div id="learning-outcomes" class="slide section level1">
<h1>Learning Outcomes</h1>
<ol style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>students should be able to demonstrate an understanding of:
<ul>
<li>mean</li>
<li>median</li>
<li>mode</li>
<li>variance</li>
<li>standard deviation</li>
<li>Normal distribution</li>
</ul></li>
</ol>
</div>
<div id="goals-of-the-presentation" class="slide section level1">
<h1>Goals of the presentation</h1>
<ol start="2" style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li><p>Demonstrate concepts using the <a href="https://www.statcan.gc.ca/eng/survey/household/3701">Labour Force Survey</a></p></li>
<li><p>R code provided is meant to:</p>
<ul>
<li>reinforce previous familiarity with R</li>
<li>demonstrate concepts</li>
</ul></li>
</ol>
</div>
<div id="central-tendency" class="slide section level1">
<h1>Central Tendency</h1>
<ul>
<li>One of the goals is to describe the world with numbers.</li>
<li>describing where the centre of a set of data is is pretty useful</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div id="mean" class="slide section level1">
<h1>Mean</h1>
<ul>
<li>most common measure of central tendency</li>
</ul>
<p><span class="math inline">\(\overline{x}=\frac{\sum_{i=1}^{N}x_{i}}{N}\)</span></p>
</div>
<div id="mean-1" class="slide section level1">
<h1>Mean</h1>
<h2 id="example">Example</h2>
<p>Load data from the Labour Force Survey</p>
<ul>
<li>These data are stored in a file-format called <code>sav</code> which is really common in the social sciences</li>
<li>loading the <code>haven</code> library provides the <code>read_sav()</code> command to read it in</li>
<li>loading the <code>labelled</code> library lets us search through variables quickly</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div id="mean-2" class="slide section level1">
<h1>Mean</h1>
<h2 id="example-1">Example</h2>
<div class="sourceCode" id="cb1"><pre class="sourceCode r"><code class="sourceCode r"><span id="cb1-1"><a href="#cb1-1"></a><span class="co">#install.packages(c(&#39;haven&#39;, &#39;labelled&#39;))</span></span>
<span id="cb1-2"><a href="#cb1-2"></a><span class="kw">library</span>(haven)</span>
<span id="cb1-3"><a href="#cb1-3"></a>lfs&lt;-<span class="kw">read_sav</span>(<span class="st">&#39;https://github.com/sjkiss/DMJN328/raw/master/Lecture_Notes/mar_11/data/lfs.sav&#39;</span>)</span></code></pre></div>
<div class="sourceCode" id="cb2"><pre class="sourceCode r"><code class="sourceCode r"><span id="cb2-1"><a href="#cb2-1"></a><span class="kw">library</span>(labelled)</span>
<span id="cb2-2"><a href="#cb2-2"></a><span class="kw">look_for</span>(lfs, <span class="st">&quot;wages&quot;</span>)</span></code></pre></div>
<pre><code>## variable label
## 36 HRLYEARN Usual hourly wages, employees only</code></pre>
</div>

<div id="median-1" class="slide section level1">
<h1>Median</h1>
<ul>
<li>Median is a different measure of central tendency</li>
<li>The value at which half of a variable is above, half is below.</li>
</ul>
<div class="sourceCode" id="cb18"><pre class="sourceCode r"><code class="sourceCode r"><span id="cb18-1"><a href="#cb18-1"></a>lfs <span class="op">%&gt;%</span></span>

<div id="measures-of-dispersion" class="slide section level1">
<h1>Measures of Dispersion</h1>
<h2 id="variance">Variance</h2>
<ul>
<li>Often not just interested in the center of the data, but the distribution</li>
</ul>
<div class="sourceCode" id="cb24"><pre class="sourceCode r"><code class="sourceCode r"><span id="cb24-1"><a href="#cb24-1"></a><span class="co">#make one class of fake data, average =75, standard deviation =1</span></span>
<span id="cb24-2"><a href="#cb24-2"></a>class1&lt;-<span class="kw">rnorm</span>(<span class="dv">100</span>, <span class="dt">mean=</span><span class="dv">75</span>, <span class="dt">sd=</span><span class="dv">1</span>)</span>
<span id="cb24-3"><a href="#cb24-3"></a><span class="co">#make a second class of fake data, average-=75, standard deviation = 10</span></span>
<span id="cb24-4"><a href="#cb24-4"></a>class2&lt;-<span class="kw">rnorm</span>(<span class="dv">100</span>, <span class="dt">mean=</span><span class="dv">75</span>, <span class="dt">sd=</span><span class="dv">10</span>)</span>
<span id="cb24-5"><a href="#cb24-5"></a><span class="co">#combine into a dataframe</span></span>
<span id="cb24-6"><a href="#cb24-6"></a>df&lt;-<span class="kw">data.frame</span>(class1, class2)</span></code></pre></div>
</div>
<div id="measures-of-dispersion-1" class="slide section level1">
<h1>Measures of Dispersion</h1>
<h2 id="variance-1">Variance</h2>
<div class="sourceCode" id="cb25"><pre class="sourceCode r"><code class="sourceCode r"><span id="cb25-1"><a href="#cb25-1"></a>df <span class="op">%&gt;%</span></span>
<span id="cb25-2"><a href="#cb25-2"></a><span class="st"> </span><span class="co">#gather into Class and Grade</span></span>

<span id="cb25-4"><a href="#cb25-4"></a><span class="st"> </span><span class="co">#Graph and facet</span></span>
<span id="cb25-5"><a href="#cb25-5"></a><span class="st"> </span><span class="kw">ggplot</span>(., <span class="kw">aes</span>(<span class="dt">x=</span>Grade))<span class="op">+</span><span class="kw">geom_histogram</span>()<span class="op">+</span><span class="kw">facet_wrap</span>(<span class="op">~</span>Class)</span></code></pre></div>

<div id="measures-of-dispersion-3" class="slide section level1">
<h1>Measures of Dispersion</h1>
<h2 id="variance-2">Variance</h2>
<ol style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>Subtract the average from each value</li>
<li>Square it to get rid of the negatives</li>
<li>Sum everything up</li>
<li>divide by the sample size.</li>
</ol>
</div>
<div id="measures-of-dispersion-4" class="slide section level1">
<h1>Measures of Dispersion</h1>
<h2 id="variance-3">Variance</h2>
<p><span class="math display">\[
s^2 = \textrm{sample variance}\\
\sum = \textrm{sum everything from the bottom to the top}\\
\overline{x} = \textrm{sample average}\\
N = \textrm{sample size}\\
\]</span></p>
<p><span class="math display">\[s^2=\frac{\sum\limits_{i=1}^N{(x_i-\overline{x})}^2}{N-1}\]</span></p>
</div>
<div id="variance-4" class="slide section level1">
<h1>Variance</h1>
<div class="sourceCode" id="cb26"><pre class="sourceCode r"><code class="sourceCode r"><span id="cb26-1"><a href="#cb26-1"></a><span class="co">#Step 1 is to subtract hte average from each value</span></span>
<span id="cb26-2"><a href="#cb26-2"></a>step1&lt;-lfs<span class="op">$</span>HRLYEARN<span class="op">-</span><span class="kw">mean</span>(lfs<span class="op">$</span>HRLYEARN, <span class="dt">na.rm=</span>T)</span>
<span id="cb26-3"><a href="#cb26-3"></a><span class="co">#step 2 is to square to get rid of the means</span></span>
<span id="cb26-4"><a href="#cb26-4"></a>step2&lt;-step1<span class="op">^</span><span class="dv">2</span></span>
<span id="cb26-5"><a href="#cb26-5"></a><span class="co">#step 3 is to sum all of the variances, na.rm=T to remove missing values</span></span>
<span id="cb26-6"><a href="#cb26-6"></a>step3&lt;-<span class="kw">sum</span>(step2, <span class="dt">na.rm=</span>T)</span>
<span id="cb26-7"><a href="#cb26-7"></a><span class="co">#step 4 is to divide by the sample size (excluding missing values)</span></span>
<span id="cb26-8"><a href="#cb26-8"></a>variance&lt;-step3<span class="op">/</span>(<span class="kw">length</span>(<span class="kw">na.omit</span>(lfs<span class="op">$</span>HRLYEARN))<span class="op">-</span><span class="dv">1</span>)</span>
<span id="cb26-9"><a href="#cb26-9"></a><span class="co">#compare with the base</span></span>
<span id="cb26-10"><a href="#cb26-10"></a><span class="kw">print</span>(variance)</span></code></pre></div>
<pre><code>## [1] 194.1875</code></pre>
<div class="sourceCode" id="cb28"><pre class="sourceCode r"><code class="sourceCode r"><span id="cb28-1"><a href="#cb28-1"></a><span class="kw">var</span>(lfs<span class="op">$</span>HRLYEARN, <span class="dt">na.rm=</span>T)</span></code></pre></div>
<pre><code>## [1] 194.1875</code></pre>
</div>
<div id="standard-deviation" class="slide section level1">
<h1>Standard Deviation</h1>
<ul>
<li>variance is expressed in units squared</li>
<li>unsquare it gives us a standard deviation</li>
</ul>
<p><span class="math display">\[s=\sqrt{\frac{\sum\limits_{i=1}^N{(x_i-\overline{x})}^2}{N-1}}\]</span></p>
<ul>
<li>Commonly we talk about something being 1 standard deviation away, or two standard deviations away.</li>
<li>Standard deviation is a number that describes the averge distance from the average in the units that variable is taken.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div id="distributions" class="slide section level1">
<h1>Distributions</h1>
<ul>
<li>Data come in different types (categorical, numeric)</li>
<li>there are different processes in the universe that generate data</li>
<li>data follow different distributions
<ul>
<li>Recall from ** The Joy of Stats** the importance of a distribution</li>
</ul></li>
</ul>
</div>
<div id="distributions-1" class="slide section level1">
<h1>Distributions</h1>
<ol style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>Normal distribution
<ul>
<li>mean = median = mode</li>
<li>contstantly reoccurring pattern in nature</li>
</ul></li>
</ol>
</div>
<div id="distributions-2" class="slide section level1">
<h1>Distributions</h1>
<ol style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>Normal distribution</li>
</ol>
<div class="sourceCode" id="cb30"><pre class="sourceCode r"><code class="sourceCode r"><span id="cb30-1"><a href="#cb30-1"></a><span class="co">#use rnorm to generate 10000 random numbers according to the normal distribution</span></span>
<span id="cb30-2"><a href="#cb30-2"></a><span class="co">#mean of 1000 and standard deviation of 500</span></span>
<span id="cb30-3"><a href="#cb30-3"></a>var1&lt;-<span class="kw">rnorm</span>(<span class="dv">10000</span>, <span class="dt">mean=</span><span class="dv">1000</span>, <span class="dt">sd=</span><span class="dv">500</span>)</span>
<span id="cb30-4"><a href="#cb30-4"></a><span class="co">#make into a data frame</span></span>
<span id="cb30-5"><a href="#cb30-5"></a>df&lt;-<span class="kw">data.frame</span>(var1)</span>
<span id="cb30-6"><a href="#cb30-6"></a><span class="co">#graph a histogram</span></span>
<span id="cb30-7"><a href="#cb30-7"></a><span class="kw">ggplot</span>(df, <span class="kw">aes</span>(<span class="dt">x=</span>var1))<span class="op">+</span><span class="kw">geom_histogram</span>()<span class="op">+</span><span class="kw">theme_bw</span>()<span class="op">+</span><span class="kw">labs</span>(<span class="dt">title=</span><span class="st">&quot;Randomly Generated Normal Distribution&quot;</span>)</span></code></pre></div>

<h1>Distributions</h1>

<li>Uniform Distribution</li>
</ol>
<div class="sourceCode" id="cb32"><pre class="sourceCode r"><code class="sourceCode r"><span id="cb32-1"><a href="#cb32-1"></a><span class="co">#Sample a number from 1 to 6 (like on a die roll), 10000 times</span></span>
<span id="cb32-2"><a href="#cb32-2"></a>var1&lt;-<span class="kw">sample</span>(<span class="dv">1</span><span class="op">:</span><span class="dv">6</span>, <span class="dv">10000</span>, <span class="dt">replace=</span>T)</span>
<span id="cb32-3"><a href="#cb32-3"></a><span class="co">#turn into a dataframe (die)</span></span>
<span id="cb32-4"><a href="#cb32-4"></a>die&lt;-<span class="kw">data.frame</span>(var1)</span>
<span id="cb32-5"><a href="#cb32-5"></a><span class="co">#Graph as a</span></span>
<span id="cb32-6"><a href="#cb32-6"></a><span class="kw">ggplot</span>(die, <span class="kw">aes</span>(<span class="dt">x=</span>var1))<span class="op">+</span></span>
<span id="cb32-7"><a href="#cb32-7"></a><span class="st"> </span><span class="co">#as a barplot, counting the numbr of times each number occurs</span></span>
<span id="cb32-8"><a href="#cb32-8"></a><span class="st"> </span><span class="kw">geom_bar</span>(<span class="dt">stat=</span><span class="st">&quot;count&quot;</span>)<span class="op">+</span></span>
<span id="cb32-9"><a href="#cb32-9"></a><span class="st"> </span><span class="co">#turn it black and white</span></span>
<span id="cb32-10"><a href="#cb32-10"></a><span class="st"> </span><span class="kw">theme_bw</span>()<span class="op">+</span></span>
<span id="cb32-11"><a href="#cb32-11"></a><span class="st"> </span><span class="co">#give some labels</span></span>

<div id="normal-distribution" class="slide section level1">
<h1>Normal Distribution</h1>
<ul>
<li>an absolute key feature of the normal distribution is that approximately:
<ul>
<li>68% of all cases lie within one standard deviation of the mean;</li>
<li>95% of cases lie within two standard deviations of the mean and</li>
<li>99% of cases lie within three standard deviations from the mean.</li>
</ul></li>
</ul>
</div>
